  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3cc359e7-e3f1-43c7-92c3-0e1bd4382e9e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="review_159669258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159669258" />
    <a title="Fabian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1036893-fabian"><img alt="Fabian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514061293p2/1036893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159669258?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fabian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fabian" href="/user/show/1036893-fabian">Fabian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1036893-fabian?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159669258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14189524854635031868">The Tesseract by Alex Garland is a novel that lets the reader wonder at his/her own insignificance. It is a theme that's already been implanted there, in the modern reader’s sophisticated brain, by Voltaire, and made new again by this generation’s collective and personal psyche, which is quite enormous/ambitious in scope. It’s no travesty to say that the society of 2011 is somewhat the intended dream of our future from way before the millennium--that is, we are living the 2011 version according </span>
  <span id="freeText14189524854635031868" style="display:none">The Tesseract by Alex Garland is a novel that lets the reader wonder at his/her own insignificance. It is a theme that's already been implanted there, in the modern reader’s sophisticated brain, by Voltaire, and made new again by this generation’s collective and personal psyche, which is quite enormous/ambitious in scope. It’s no travesty to say that the society of 2011 is somewhat the intended dream of our future from way before the millennium--that is, we are living the 2011 version according to 1999, the very oracular year. There is an omnipresent ghost that hovers above it all, called Globalization, and this specter is felt everywhere: from the smallest villages of Thailand to the most industrialized cosmopolitan cities of the U.S. This current feeling had been hinted at way before it even got here. <br /><br />Alex Garland is a remarkable writer. He says that there is in life, in his novel, “something… you are not equipped to understand.” The Tesseract is "[that] thing unraveled, but not the thing itself.” (249) This conclusion is reached only after having read the three distinct vignettes which finally come together in the impressive fourth act. Cohesiveness is found once all stories are put together, like a jigsaw puzzle. The three stories are completely different from one another in tone and style, though the writer’s voice is identifiable &amp; easy to read (but it strays from the comprehensible by oftentimes entering the realm of the poetic). <br /><br />This writer has very little to hide: he is definitely more about exposing secrets than hiding them (as opposed to countless other great modern British novels, including Ishiguru’s Never Let Me Go, Hollinghurst’s The Line of Beauty or anything Julian Barnes). The Tesseract is a terrific Masterpiece.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14189524854635031868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_139755386" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139755386" />
    <a title="Maciek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek"><img alt="Maciek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280839159p2/2969647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139755386?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maciek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maciek" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek">Maciek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140258424" href="/book/show/8763.The_Tesseract">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=own-in-paperback">own-in-paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139755386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17018781494475498037"><i>The Tesseract</i> suffers from the case of the infamous sophomore jinx simply because it is in no way like Garland's fabulous debut novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/607639.The_Beach' title='The Beach by Alex Garland' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Beach</a>.<br/>The voice is completely different. <i>The Beach</i> was linear, almost cinematic in scope, a rather conventional novel; <i>The Tesseract</i> is experimental, and the writing dry, sparse and moody. The novel is set in Manila, and through three separate, non-linear narratives it shows the story of three groups of people who would normally never met, but whom fate has co</span>
  <span id="freeText17018781494475498037" style="display:none"><i>The Tesseract</i> suffers from the case of the infamous sophomore jinx simply because it is in no way like Garland's fabulous debut novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/607639.The_Beach" title="The Beach by Alex Garland" rel="nofollow noopener">The Beach</a>.<br />The voice is completely different. <i>The Beach</i> was linear, almost cinematic in scope, a rather conventional novel; <i>The Tesseract</i> is experimental, and the writing dry, sparse and moody. The novel is set in Manila, and through three separate, non-linear narratives it shows the story of three groups of people who would normally never met, but whom fate has connected in a most violent way.<br />There are good bits in <i>The Tesseract</i>, but as a whole the novel falls rather short. The characters aren't particularly memorable and the concept of the tesseract is thrown in almost desperately, as a bit of novelty could shed an entirely new light on the familiar concept of the same incident being related by different people. Garland offers us a bunch of quick, skilfully drawn sketches and fluently switches between them, much like Quentin Tarantino did in <i>Pulp Fiction</i>. <br />While not as spellbinding as <i>The Beach</i>, <i>The Tesseract</i> is fast paced and has its moments (The Filipino love story, the man who buys dreams) but as a whole the novel feels like a concept that wasn't entirely fleshed out. It feels more like a transitional piece, of a writer in-developement, who has estabilished himself in one field and doesn't fear trying new things. It is sad that Garland seems to have abandoned writing novels and now concentrates on adapting them for the screen. Maybe he only had one great work in him? <i>The Tesseract</i> unfortunately offers no answer. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17018781494475498037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_395572936" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/395572936" />
    <a title="Linna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3226530-linna"><img alt="Linna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330731364p2/3226530.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/395572936?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linna" href="/user/show/3226530-linna">Linna</a>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<div id="review_840942213" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/840942213" />
    <a title="N.J. Ramsden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27040673-n-j-ramsden"><img alt="N.J. Ramsden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483107765p2/27040673.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/840942213?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="N.J. Ramsden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="N.J. Ramsden" href="/user/show/27040673-n-j-ramsden">N.J. Ramsden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="paperback 9780670870165" href="/book/show/410204.The_Tesseract">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27040673-n-j-ramsden?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer840942213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1503240225059392437">Another example of a book smothered with praise from high-profile names, yet totally failing to deliver anything but a kind of intellectual indigestion. And not from richness.<br/><br/>What's wrong with it? We can start with Garland's enormously pretentious* explanation of his title. I won't waste time copying it out. Let's just say it's bullshit. And totally unnecessary. If you have a good narrative and a good title, neither requires justification. Sadly The Tesseract lacks at least the former.<br/><br/>The story </span>
  <span id="freeText1503240225059392437" style="display:none">Another example of a book smothered with praise from high-profile names, yet totally failing to deliver anything but a kind of intellectual indigestion. And not from richness.<br /><br />What's wrong with it? We can start with Garland's enormously pretentious* explanation of his title. I won't waste time copying it out. Let's just say it's bullshit. And totally unnecessary. If you have a good narrative and a good title, neither requires justification. Sadly The Tesseract lacks at least the former.<br /><br />The story could have been a good one in more accomplished hands, but Garland renders it dull and lifeless, and seems insistent on populating his novel with the kind of weak clichés more commonly found in bad made-for-TV afternoon thrillers. The whole thing becomes laughably bad. Then the plot itself - we've seen this "multiple threads that seem disparate but OH WAIT THEY ALL MESH AT THE END" except here it's just like having two people meet in the queue at a supermarket, never speak, and go home separately. Garlands utterly fails to make anything even vaguely interesting or satisfying out of a premise that requires more intelligent handling to say something worthwhile. This feels like a very lazy way to jam together a few short pieces and not have any better way to do it. But hey, let's stick a pretentious intro about a fancy title on there and hope nobody notices.<br /><br />tl;dr: bilge.<br /><br />* I hesitate almost entirely to use the word "pretentious" about as many thing as possible that seem to garner its use. I don't use it as shorthand for "tried to achieve greatness but failed", or "I don't get it so it must be crap". I use it to imply something *pretends* to something it blatantly is not, does not really try to be, and could never be if it were injected with a ton of crack. Sad to say this review needs it twice.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1503240225059392437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aimee Capinpuyan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aimee Capinpuyan" href="/user/show/15910140-aimee-capinpuyan">Aimee Capinpuyan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer580461626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18290160466049815357">Set in the Philippines, The Tesseract pretends to be some action thriller novel that takes the reader through the lives of various people. It was a largely forgetful book. The protagonist, I think his name was Simon (see? I can't even remember) was bland. Every other character was bland too. Thankfully the Philippines was given some life in this book. Garland nicely described the scenery here, and he doesn't sugar coat it as to make it sound ridiculous.<br/><br/>The plot was really dumb. The climax wasn't</span>
  <span id="freeText18290160466049815357" style="display:none">Set in the Philippines, The Tesseract pretends to be some action thriller novel that takes the reader through the lives of various people. It was a largely forgetful book. The protagonist, I think his name was Simon (see? I can't even remember) was bland. Every other character was bland too. Thankfully the Philippines was given some life in this book. Garland nicely described the scenery here, and he doesn't sugar coat it as to make it sound ridiculous.<br /><br />The plot was really dumb. The climax wasn't especially climactic. The drama not dramatic. Some of the action was pointless and it sometimes made me wonder "What the hell were you on when you wrote this, guy?" I didn't get how the stories came together. <br /><br />I did enjoy the scenes at Hotel Patay. Those were rather suspenseful and expertly told. But everything went downhill from there. <br /><br />And yes. The Hotel is named Hotel Patay. Just goes to show how much thought went into this novel, because Patay is the Filipino word for DEAD. WHAT KIND OF PHILIPPINE HOTEL WOULD BE NAMED HOTEL DEAD!?<br /><br />Yes I know this review sucks. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18290160466049815357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer436498273" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8886507577526140887">I have just finished this book this morning and I, like many others, picked up this book after thoroughly enjoying his previous novel The Beach. When starting The Tesseract, you can clearly feel the similarities between this book and his previous but The Tesseract quickly becomes its own story. The book follows several different characters and jumps around within the timeline. It starts with Sean in a `roach infested hotel' as he awaits the arrival of local gangster Don Pepe. Next we have a Fili</span>
  <span id="freeText8886507577526140887" style="display:none">I have just finished this book this morning and I, like many others, picked up this book after thoroughly enjoying his previous novel The Beach. When starting The Tesseract, you can clearly feel the similarities between this book and his previous but The Tesseract quickly becomes its own story. The book follows several different characters and jumps around within the timeline. It starts with Sean in a `roach infested hotel' as he awaits the arrival of local gangster Don Pepe. Next we have a Filipino family living out in the suburbs in Manila and finally we have some street kids living their lives in a rough environment. At first, these situations all seem completely unrelated but the links become clear towards the end of the book. I did enjoy this read but you can't help but compare it to his previous novel which had such success.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7542643613962313786">A reread from fifteen years ago? Since that time, Garland has morphed into one of the strongest screenwriters in Hollywood. When he hits, he hits hard. He rarely misses. <br/><br/>This novel is fine. There’s a very turn of the century/Fight Club era Palahniuk by way of Guy Ritchie directed film style to the writing that comes about with the extremely fractured narrative and the frequent use of synecdoche. It makes the novel feel dated in an unflattering way. At its heart the novel is still entertaining th</span>
  <span id="freeText7542643613962313786" style="display:none">A reread from fifteen years ago? Since that time, Garland has morphed into one of the strongest screenwriters in Hollywood. When he hits, he hits hard. He rarely misses. <br /><br />This novel is fine. There’s a very turn of the century/Fight Club era Palahniuk by way of Guy Ritchie directed film style to the writing that comes about with the extremely fractured narrative and the frequent use of synecdoche. It makes the novel feel dated in an unflattering way. At its heart the novel is still entertaining though, and it does hold some of the surprises that Garland continues to cook up as a writer and director of films. <br /><br />3 stars. Maybe 3.25?</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2336726752370354037">I have no idea what I just read, to be honest. If someone asked me to give a short summary of this book, I wouldn't be able to give even one sentence. <br/>There are multiple stories within this novel: one takes place in just one night, starts with an American named Sean shooting one of the big mafia bosses in Manila and his bodyguard. Sean is then being chased by two other bodyguards, ends up holding a young mother of two, Rosa, hostage, and all that is being witnessed by two street kids, Vincente (</span>
  <span id="freeText2336726752370354037" style="display:none">I have no idea what I just read, to be honest. If someone asked me to give a short summary of this book, I wouldn't be able to give even one sentence. <br />There are multiple stories within this novel: one takes place in just one night, starts with an American named Sean shooting one of the big mafia bosses in Manila and his bodyguard. Sean is then being chased by two other bodyguards, ends up holding a young mother of two, Rosa, hostage, and all that is being witnessed by two street kids, Vincente (Cento) and Totoy.<br />The other story lines take us back to Rosa's childhood and her first love, to Vincente's past and how he became a street kid, with no family. <br />There are things in this novel that are still confusing the crap out of me, even after reading it. For example, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Did Lito, Rosa's first love, really threw acid on her newborn son at her father's funeral? I don't get it  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> . I also don't really understand the role of Alfredo, a PhD student, a very rich PhD student, who is collecting the dreams of street kids in order to write his dissertation. Also <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ we eventually learn that his wife committed suicide by jumping for the 30th floor of their apartment, but we don't know anything about her, or why did she do it  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. If the author wasn't really going to provide us background of Alfredo and his wife, why put them in the book in the first place? <br /></span>

<div id="review_207592081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/207592081" />
    <a title="Dan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5928923-dan"><img alt="Dan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312147980p2/5928923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/207592081?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan" href="/user/show/5928923-dan">Dan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141031781" href="/book/show/2201460.The_Tesseract">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207592081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7633478159198628384">I read "The Beach" quite a few years ago and liked it very much. I mostly forgot about Alex Garland for a while until I stumbled across this one and thought I'd give it a try.<br/><br/>It's a very well written book, done up in three main arcs: a young British traveller, a wife and mother in suburban Manilla and a young boy living on the streets. It's peppered with other characters, but these are your three main ones. Each has their story told, and each of their stories all intersect in a well thought out </span>
  <span id="freeText7633478159198628384" style="display:none">I read "The Beach" quite a few years ago and liked it very much. I mostly forgot about Alex Garland for a while until I stumbled across this one and thought I'd give it a try.<br /><br />It's a very well written book, done up in three main arcs: a young British traveller, a wife and mother in suburban Manilla and a young boy living on the streets. It's peppered with other characters, but these are your three main ones. Each has their story told, and each of their stories all intersect in a well thought out way.<br /><br />The main metaphor of this book is the shape of a tesseract, which is a hypercube unravelled. Garland's statement is that you can see the tesseract, but can't see the hypercube after it's been unravelled. You can see the parts when they're spread out, but not what the whole is. It's a great metaphor for this book, and if you approach it with this in mind, you'll not be too jarred by the jumps from story to story.<br /><br />Great read, and I'm looking forward to picking up some more of Mr. Garland's books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7633478159198628384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="James Crisp" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/106240448-james-crisp"><img alt="James Crisp" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3399933101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6713756530624404999">I love all things Alex Garland, and this was the one piece of work solely by him I had yet to read/watch. (After - The Beach, The Coma, Ex Machina, Annihilation, Devs) and I have to say I was extremely disappointed. I came into this book really wanting to enjoy it but only managed to get just about half way through. Bar one exciting moment, the book just laboured on confusing time frames, and frankly dull characters. The short sequence and flashback/flash-forward style of writing was somewhat ja</span>
  <span id="freeText6713756530624404999" style="display:none">I love all things Alex Garland, and this was the one piece of work solely by him I had yet to read/watch. (After - The Beach, The Coma, Ex Machina, Annihilation, Devs) and I have to say I was extremely disappointed. I came into this book really wanting to enjoy it but only managed to get just about half way through. Bar one exciting moment, the book just laboured on confusing time frames, and frankly dull characters. The short sequence and flashback/flash-forward style of writing was somewhat jarring - and meant I didn’t really know what I was reading most of the time. There were subplots layered onto subplots and it just all seemed to disappear into tangents that were unsatisfying to read. Real shame as everything else Garland has touched is gold.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6713756530624404999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

The book tells the story of Rosa, a Filipino mother, and a few gangsters chasing another gangster through part of Manila. I have yet to find gun play convincing in fiction. Too many tedious details.<br/><br/>The novel is supposed to be an unfolding of tesseract, a depiction of a projection of a three dimensional object into a fourth dimension.</span>

<div id="review_404012299" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404012299" />
    <a title="Eliza Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12382681-eliza-victoria"><img alt="Eliza Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505983536p2/12382681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/404012299?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eliza Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eliza Victoria" href="/user/show/12382681-eliza-victoria">Eliza Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer404012299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8508642563623368859">The novel opens like a thriller. A British seaman waits in a seedy Manila hotel for a rich Filipino mafioso. He notices several things almost all at once: the dead phone, the peephole covered from the outside, rusty blood spatters on the bedsheet, a gunshot hole in the ceiling, a room with no exit. The Filipino don is in a car with his crew, weaving through the dark streets of the city, and the seaman takes out his gun, believing that they are coming to kill him.<br/><br/>Gunshots and a chase – the staple</span>
  <span id="freeText8508642563623368859" style="display:none">The novel opens like a thriller. A British seaman waits in a seedy Manila hotel for a rich Filipino mafioso. He notices several things almost all at once: the dead phone, the peephole covered from the outside, rusty blood spatters on the bedsheet, a gunshot hole in the ceiling, a room with no exit. The Filipino don is in a car with his crew, weaving through the dark streets of the city, and the seaman takes out his gun, believing that they are coming to kill him.<br /><br />Gunshots and a chase – the staples of action movies – but what reeled me in were the characters and their personal tragedies, and the fact that Garland set his story of one, stifling night in Manila.<br /><br />Such a pleasure to read a familiar world, made new and intriguing by Garland’s compassionate treatment of his characters, his insights, and his crisp, clear, high-energy prose: Back in his room, some of the wetter stains on the street began to glow red as the sun dropped from the sky. Dropped, because the sun didn’t sink in these parts. At six-fifteen, the elastic that kept it suspended started to stretch, and at six-thirty the elastic snapped. Then you had just ten minutes as the orange ellipse plummeted out of view, and the next thing you knew it was night. You had to watch out for that in Manila. Ten minutes to catch a cab to the right side of town if you were on the wrong side.<br /><br />Garland writes about Manila (and Negros and Quezon Province, in some flashbacks) as both an insider and an outsider. An outsider because he wasn’t born here, an insider because he’s been here, and has (presumably) learned much about the language and the culture. Because the familiar is made foreign (and the foreign made familiar) he sees and describes things I don’t normally pay attention to, like that rapidly sinking sun.<br /><br />He obviously had fun with using Filipino words for places: Patay, Sugat, Sayang, Sarap. He also liked mentioning Filipino brand names whenever he could. Magnolia, Bench, Inquirer.<br /><br />There are errors. You don’t write “Yes, po” if in your head the characters are speaking in Filipino (better stick with “Yes” or write the proper “Opo”), and you don’t say “Mang Don Pepe” because that’s an awkward double honorific (unless of course “Don” is the person’s first name).<br /><br />But other than that, this is a highly readable book.<br /><br />Very poignant. Unputdownable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8508642563623368859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_15240135" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15240135" />
    <a title="Nancy Oakes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/900340-nancy-oakes"><img alt="Nancy Oakes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507555979p2/900340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15240135?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy Oakes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy Oakes" href="/user/show/900340-nancy-oakes">Nancy Oakes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15240135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4568435864999368433">Set in the Philippines, the story focuses on three very different groups of people from different walks of life, and who probably should never in real life have any reason to meet each other, but do here through a bizarre set of circumstances. Throughout the narrative, I got the feeling that each of these people have no way to understand why these things are happening to them; they just are -- and it's just a matter of timing and circumstance, with no rhyme nor reason -- and that even at the end</span>
  <span id="freeText4568435864999368433" style="display:none">Set in the Philippines, the story focuses on three very different groups of people from different walks of life, and who probably should never in real life have any reason to meet each other, but do here through a bizarre set of circumstances. Throughout the narrative, I got the feeling that each of these people have no way to understand why these things are happening to them; they just are -- and it's just a matter of timing and circumstance, with no rhyme nor reason -- and that even at the end, the whole "unraveling" if you will, I was still left with the notion, as one of the characters was so fond of quoting, "that's just the way it was." So really, if you're looking for some kind of explanation of it all, my advice is not to.<br /><br />As in his first book, "The Beach," Garland starts his story in a run-down hotel room, where the character Sean notices that the peephole has been covered over. He also notices that he is in a room where the sheets have bloodstains, the phone is decorated with perfectly made circles made by cigarette burns and he deduces that he's staying in a room where a torturer once stayed. As he ponders all of the reasons why he's making this conclusion, and what scenarios may have occurred to make the bloodstains, he's also thinking about the meeting with Don Pepe, who runs some kind of Mafia-type piracy ring where he deals with merchant marine sea captains. Don Pepe arrives early and Sean jumps to the conclusion that he's going to be killed and tries to stay ahead of the game by being prepared to shoot first. He succeeds in killing Don Pepe and his right-hand man, but this leaves two more of Don Pepe's men, who chase him through the streets of Manila. His path will intersect with that of two street kids, and it will also intersect with that of Rosa, a doctor with two children, a husband and a mother, who live in a quiet upscale suburb there.<br /><br />The story flows very well even though the narrative is not exactly linear; everything intersects and the chapters weave in and out of narratives of the various characters' stories. The characterization is excellent, making it possible for the readers to get into the characters' lives.<br /><br />Very tense at times; recommended . </span>
  <a data-text-id="4568435864999368433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_179579183" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179579183" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5449722-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308023010p2/5449722.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/179579183?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/5449722-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5449722-barbara?shelf=fiction-literature">fiction-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179579183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2528977551457028948">“Tesseract” – a four-dimensional hypercube with all equal sides and right angles; the author includes in the definition the “unraveling” of same. This book is three separate tales, taking place over the span of both a few hours and several years. The first involves an emissary for a smuggler who is behind on his protection payments, awaiting the arrival of an unhappy enforcer in a Manila hotel room. The second deals with a young doctor, a happily married mother of two who, nonetheless, mourns a </span>
  <span id="freeText2528977551457028948" style="display:none">“Tesseract” – a four-dimensional hypercube with all equal sides and right angles; the author includes in the definition the “unraveling” of same. This book is three separate tales, taking place over the span of both a few hours and several years. The first involves an emissary for a smuggler who is behind on his protection payments, awaiting the arrival of an unhappy enforcer in a Manila hotel room. The second deals with a young doctor, a happily married mother of two who, nonetheless, mourns a lost love from her youth. The third is about a psychology student preparing his thesis on Manila’s street children while he grieves his wife’s suicide. The creation of the tesseract is achieved through the development of each character’s past, and the deft interweaving that connects their present lives. The unraveling is a bit trickier; the reader must decide if it is in the conclusion of the book, the final chapter, in which the author reveals to us the ultimate fate of each character. Or, if, in fact, the entire story represents a sort of unraveling, as the characters’ lives shift and change, as they relinquish the past and come to terms with the present. Interesting book, enjoyable read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2528977551457028948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_475703346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/475703346" />
    <a title="Joy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3041102-joy"><img alt="Joy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398873705p2/3041102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/475703346?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joy" href="/user/show/3041102-joy">Joy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3041102-joy?shelf=around-the-world-in-80-books">around-the-world-in-80-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer475703346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5583830686572173094">Alex Garland's The Tesseract is a story of layers. Which I'm sure if you knew the definition of the word "tesseract" [also called an 8-cell or regular octachoron or cubic prism, is the four-dimensional analog of the cube; the tesseract is to the cube as the cube is to the square], you may have already assumed as much. I did not know the definition of this word. Nor did I fully grasp this story until the last 15 pages. <br/><br/>There are many things happening at once…a European man killing for his life, a</span>
  <span id="freeText5583830686572173094" style="display:none">Alex Garland's The Tesseract is a story of layers. Which I'm sure if you knew the definition of the word "tesseract" [also called an 8-cell or regular octachoron or cubic prism, is the four-dimensional analog of the cube; the tesseract is to the cube as the cube is to the square], you may have already assumed as much. I did not know the definition of this word. Nor did I fully grasp this story until the last 15 pages. <br /><br />There are many things happening at once…a European man killing for his life, a Filipino woman raising her children as her husband tries to make it home from work, street children sharing their dreams with a PhD student collecting research. If you are thinking those story lines sound random, they are. But the end is worth the read. <br /><br />Alex Garland does a great job of moving these story lines, and weaving a narrative for a lesser author, would be a mess. This was a relatively short &amp; fast read, and satisfying in the end. And a glimpse into Filipino culture, from the perspective of foreigners and locals, which I truly enjoyed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5583830686572173094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

However, overall I definitely liked this book and, as it was the first of Garland's that I've read, I'll have to seek </span>
  <span id="freeText12257367636964556121" style="display:none">Despite the fact that almost nothing good happens to any of the characters in the book, I really enjoyed reading "The Tesseract." Sometimes all the elements lost a little of that power as Alex Garland pushed them together into one conclusion. However, overall I definitely liked this book and, as it was the first of Garland's that I've read, I'll have to seek out some of his other novels. </span>

<div id="review_2539803425" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2539803425" />
    <a title="Steven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5749733-steven"><img alt="Steven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370373980p2/5749733.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2539803425?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steven" href="/user/show/5749733-steven">Steven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140258424" href="/book/show/8763.The_Tesseract">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2539803425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17641379933213389982">Interesting book.<br/><br/>What I liked: the momentum/pace (of the first section especially), the details of the characters, the loose ends/non-sequiturs in the plot, the fact that the book takes an action-movie-esque setup and deconstructs it as a sort of literary character study/metaphysical musing on meaninglessness.<br/><br/>What I didn't like: the pacing is uneven, the characters are often too pat and don't have realistic rough edges (and they felt very 'Western' in some of their speech/thought, most especiall</span>
  <span id="freeText17641379933213389982" style="display:none">Interesting book.<br /><br />What I liked: the momentum/pace (of the first section especially), the details of the characters, the loose ends/non-sequiturs in the plot, the fact that the book takes an action-movie-esque setup and deconstructs it as a sort of literary character study/metaphysical musing on meaninglessness.<br /><br />What I didn't like: the pacing is uneven, the characters are often too pat and don't have realistic rough edges (and they felt very 'Western' in some of their speech/thought, most especially Vincente, which, while I can 'get' the point about individualism, I simply did not buy that this street kid was waxing so philosophical and SO eloquent so often, whereas the rest of the characters seemed to speak much more in line with their backgrounds and environments), the philosophical 'points' were sometimes a bit too on-the-nose, sections were over-written, and the typeset. <br /><br />This book feels like it should've been a character-sketch novella that was stretched into a 'novel.' I would've liked it to stay shorter and focus on the elements of character *essential* to the story (though one could argue none are in a way, but that's too pretentious for me) or go a bit longer and delve further into some of the characters beyond mere coincidences (e.g., for me, Rosa's husband was someone interesting whose backstory was nearly completely ignored).<br /><br />The tesseract was an unnecessary device, and it just felt pretentious. It would've worked exactly the same, in terms of emotional impact/philosophical point, if it had been left out entirely. I would've enjoyed the black dog for all the depressive connotations which aren't explicitly alluded to in the book, but that for me would've felt more 'authentic' than the tesseract in a book where the religion and the philosophizing felt ... forced.<br /><br />Overall though the writing was pretty good and I like what he did, I just feel like it could've been executed more messily to be a bit grittier not in tone but in the character explorations.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17641379933213389982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2158688574" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2158688574" />
    <a title="Steve Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30695734-steve-johnson"><img alt="Steve Johnson" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2158688574?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve Johnson" href="/user/show/30695734-steve-johnson">Steve Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2158688574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1339882701232421717">Alex Garland is a great writer, for sure. I was engaged by this book almost the entire time. Even though the plot feels very small scale (only involving a number of people), Garland has no trouble creating tense moments. To me his writing style is very pleasant and there are definitely some images that were put into my mind by this book that I will not soon forget. I particularly enjoyed the physics-related explanations, they felt very intuitive which is always a good accomplishment for a writer</span>
  <span id="freeText1339882701232421717" style="display:none">Alex Garland is a great writer, for sure. I was engaged by this book almost the entire time. Even though the plot feels very small scale (only involving a number of people), Garland has no trouble creating tense moments. To me his writing style is very pleasant and there are definitely some images that were put into my mind by this book that I will not soon forget. I particularly enjoyed the physics-related explanations, they felt very intuitive which is always a good accomplishment for a writer.<br /><br />However in the end this novel also disappointed me in certain ways, to me it didn't feel as grand, important or thought-provoking as I had hoped it would. The ending was a bit of a let-down for me as well. It's not a book I would easily recommend to others, though I am glad to have read it myself. It did make me think, though perhaps not in the ways I had expected. The novel does feel like it has its own style and it was very easy for me to imagine the events happening and the characters existing in this book. But I can't help but feel let down a little at the end. I'd rate 3.5/5 stars, mainly because I was so engaged by it and wanted to keep on reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1339882701232421717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2643804468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2643804468" />
    <a title="Tony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/151601-tony"><img alt="Tony" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365730769p2/151601.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2643804468?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tony" href="/user/show/151601-tony">Tony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/151601-tony?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/151601-tony?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/151601-tony?shelf=own-loanable">own-loanable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/151601-tony?shelf=setting-asia">setting-asia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2643804468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3735367386609812133">Very interesting and well-written set of interwoven events and stories centered on a single day in Manila. It starts with an English sailor waiting in a hyperdingy hotel to meet with a local mobster. As he waits he becomes more and more convinced he is about to be executed. This is intercut with the mobster in the car with his retinue treading on verbal eggshells. The two meet in an explosive climax, whereupon the book shifts to the story of a woman putting her kids to sleep. This leads to the s</span>
  <span id="freeText3735367386609812133" style="display:none">Very interesting and well-written set of interwoven events and stories centered on a single day in Manila. It starts with an English sailor waiting in a hyperdingy hotel to meet with a local mobster. As he waits he becomes more and more convinced he is about to be executed. This is intercut with the mobster in the car with his retinue treading on verbal eggshells. The two meet in an explosive climax, whereupon the book shifts to the story of a woman putting her kids to sleep. This leads to the story of her childhood in a coastal village, her the discovery of love, and we gradually learn how she came to be in Manila, married and with kids. As she talks on a cell phone to her husband, street kids throw some nails in the road puncturing his tire and delaying his arrival home. This segues into the story of two street kids and the psychological researcher who tapes their dreams. At the end, all three stories converge into a brief, bloody resolution of sorts. Garland is definitely a talented writer and I will think about reading his first book, The Beach--which I have avoided as it looks very shallow and annoying.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3735367386609812133" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2736601757" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2736601757" />
    <a title="Dem" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8416342-dem"><img alt="Dem" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395010646p2/8416342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2736601757?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dem" href="/user/show/8416342-dem">Dem</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2736601757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14881442506796237580">...wow. <br/><br/>I understand some of the negative reviews, but this is not a conventional novel. It masterfully and enigmatically darts through time, and from beginning to end the main arc takes no time at all, but the novel spans several generations in flashback. I have not often been so impressed by the mere structure of a novel. It is periodically confusing, but each confusion is given a payoff either literal or existential. An incredibly intelligent book, whose plot is ultimately about the lack of p</span>
  <span id="freeText14881442506796237580" style="display:none">...wow. <br /><br />I understand some of the negative reviews, but this is not a conventional novel. It masterfully and enigmatically darts through time, and from beginning to end the main arc takes no time at all, but the novel spans several generations in flashback. I have not often been so impressed by the mere structure of a novel. It is periodically confusing, but each confusion is given a payoff either literal or existential. An incredibly intelligent book, whose plot is ultimately about the lack of plot: the way isolated sequences of events can link, and have long reaching ramifications, but whose meanings can never be understood by the participants within, due to the limits of our own perspectives.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14881442506796237580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3527216799" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Berengaria di Rossi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/120722719-berengaria-di-rossi"><img alt="Berengaria di Rossi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598888192p2/120722719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3527216799?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Berengaria di Rossi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Berengaria di Rossi" href="/user/show/120722719-berengaria-di-rossi">Berengaria di Rossi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/120722719-berengaria-di-rossi?shelf=loved-these">loved-these</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3527216799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17225095646126093785">I was totally blown away by this experimental novel. As a writer myself, I can honestly say Garland solves a number of very difficult plotting and structural problems with astounding skill. That's something that might not be noticed by a casual reader reading for story only. I literally put the novel down and applauded at one point, I was so impressed by his grace and dexterity. <br/><br/>My only critique is that the middle section is too long and takes in too much backstory of that character. That's all.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1729674439" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1729674439" />
    <a title="Beth Wilson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46778506-beth-wilson"><img alt="Beth Wilson" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1729674439?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Wilson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Wilson" href="/user/show/46778506-beth-wilson">Beth Wilson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1729674439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8620998460508544565">I enjoyed the idea of a tesseract and the collision of each of the characters in the story. A tesseract with its understandable geometry or at least an ordered way of looking at a shape (I suppose the 'easiest' way for us to compute 4d....) puts forward the idea life should have obvious cause and effect: a plan. To then bring in Alfredo's interest in dreams, the metaphysical and space really see-sawed the emotion of nitty gritty real life and the relative pointlessness of our little lives!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Htd3UjqZWmb5qDd4RGGUEo06Gv9AIi6IevHKuYMA32jFflnxbDNg+Qwi43JOUF/o6zRwR/CYG75hfc4P36xqdw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jb/2mHAR/gwRKNnlxHtvlBAHTDdH9zI8T9cZ2mlhzo9WFtg7JrvEk+SiDe/OSqRudgkmj/dNBwpUWx1sNc17kA==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5684.Alex_Garland">About Alex Garland</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17967757804867092060">Alex Garland (born 1970) is a British novelist, screenwriter, and director.<br/><br/>Garland is the son of political cartoonist Nick (Nicholas) Garland. He attended the independent University College School, in Hampstead, London, and the University of Manchester, where he studied art history.<br/><br/>His first novel, <i>The Beach</i>, was published in 1996 and drew on his experiences as a backpacker. The novel quickly beca</span>
  <span id="freeText17967757804867092060" style="display:none">Alex Garland (born 1970) is a British novelist, screenwriter, and director.<br /><br />Garland is the son of political cartoonist Nick (Nicholas) Garland. He attended the independent University College School, in Hampstead, London, and the University of Manchester, where he studied art history.<br /><br />His first novel, <i>The Beach</i>, was published in 1996 and drew on his experiences as a backpacker. The novel quickly became a cult classic and was made into a film by Danny Boyle, with Leonardo DiCaprio.<br /><br /><i>The Tesseract</i>, Garland's second novel, was published in 1998. This was also made into a film, starring Jonathan Rhys Meyers. In 2003, he wrote the screenplay for Danny Boyle's <i>28 Days Later</i>, starring Cillian Murphy. His third novel, <i>The Coma</i>, was published in 2004 and was illustrated with woodcuts by his father.<br /><br />In 2007 he wrote the screenplay for the film <i>Sunshine</i>—his second screenplay to be directed by Danny Boyle and star Cillian Murphy as lead. Garland also served as an executive producer on <i>28 Weeks Later</i>, the sequel to <i>28 Days Later</i>.<br /><br />Garland also wrote the first screenplay for <i>Halo</i>, the film adaptation of the successful video game franchise by Bungie Studios.<br /><br />He made his directorial debut with Ex Machina, a 2014 feature film based on his own story and screenplay.<br /><br />His partner is actress/director Paloma Baeza.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17967757804867092060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1020167-the-tesseract">Quotes from The Tesseract</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Дело в том, что галактики разбегаются в разные стороны, как точки на шарике, когда его надуваешь. У атома водорода только один протон. В капле воды сотни миллионов атомов водорода, а галактики состоят из сотен миллионов звезд.<br />Девять планет вращаются вокруг нашей звезды. Мы не центр Солнечной системы, а Солнечная система совсем не центр нашей галактики, которая в свою очередь не является центром разбегающейся Вселенной.<br />Мать Тотоя не отправится в ад, потому что она уже там. Твой отец не в аду, потому что там никого нет. Но он и не в раю, потому что там тоже никого нет. Когда шайка бандитов гонится за тобой по незнакомым улицам или ты врезаешься со скоростью двести миль в мостовую, летя вниз с небоскреба Легаспи, — после этого не происходит ровным счетом ничего.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/8868143">0 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Возьми шесть кубиков и сложи их в форме распятия. Потом возьми еще два и расположи их по обеим сторонам креста. У тебя получился тессеракт, трехмерная фигура. Но это всего лишь след четырехмерного куба.<br />Если разложить квадрат, получится линия.<br />Два измерения складываются в одно.<br />Куб складывается в крест. Три измерения превращаются в два.<br />Проекция гиперкуба дает тессеракт. Четыре измерения складываются в три.<br />Ты существуешь в трех пространственных измерениях Точно так же, как одномерный мальчик не может наблюдать двумерный квадрат, а двумерный мальчик — трехмерный куб, так и ты не можешь увидеть четырехмерный куб.<br />Четырехмерный куб есть нечто, что тебе просто не дано понять. Другое дело — тессеракт. Это уже что-то значит.<br />Так все обстоит для тебя и для меня, Сенте. Нам дано видеть только тень вещей, но не их суть.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/8868166">0 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/1020167-the-tesseract">More quotes&hellip;</a>
